I tell this because I am one to enjoy deep tissue massage and therefore dont mind a little pain w my therapeutic massages; in fact I prefer a bit of digging and manipulating. But this particular time I found it not on point- more like poking into my spine w sharp elbows way too hard.
Anyway, the second time I mysef went w my sister, we phoned in for an appt on a Sunday afternoon and requested we both have female masseuses.

I have sciatica so when I get flare ups, it requires rapid relief and Linda fit the bill.
And the bill??
Well, you certainly cannot beat $25 for an entire hour!
Well worth every penny.

< Review>
I have been attending this dental location for 30+ years and have had the practice switch hands a number of times after my original, highly skilled dentist sold his practice 15+ years ago. I was skeptical when the practice changed hands once again within two years.

I must report that I am delighted. What is very exciting to me, is that Dr. Kandar is a young dentist, though has plenty of experience, so he is up on the latest technology. Also, in this time of Covid, the office was over and above sanitary and I felt completely safe with how my dental treatment was handled.

The diagnostics were superior and I could actually see why I needed the treatment. When the treatment was executed, it was done without an ounce of pain, even the next day my teeth were not sore which really surprised me.

I also appreciate their membership which is very helpful since dental procedures are expensive and insurance is still in the dark ages. What I also loved, was the focus being on prevention, which is where it is at in my opinion. This leads me to Anna, the dental hygienist, who completely enlightened me on better ways to take care of my gums and my teeth and I thought I knew it all!

Everyone in the office is professional, kind, supportive, and knowledgeable in their area of expertise. I am especially impressed with Dr. Kandar, he takes a lot of pride in his work. I felt like he was an artist, careful and accurate. And I must say that I am very, very happy with the two new crowns that I received. They look like real teeth!

Though skeptical at first, I was delighted with my treatment. If you are looking for a dentist or are becoming discouraged with your current dentist, I highly recommend you give this dental office and their staff a try. I am sure you will be delighted you did.< /Review>

Below is my new comment from 09/19/20. My old comment above is three years old. It had five stars. The new comment has one star only.

I had been going to Dr. Chris Rodriguez, and Dr. Greg Larson previous owner,  for over ten years before he sold his practice to Dr. Mohammad Kandar . Few days ago, I had my hygienist appointment. The first thing I noticed that all old  employees were gone except one hygienist.  After my appointment, I was seen by Dr. Kandar. He is a knowledgeable, neat and eloquent guy. I was told hat I would need a new filling. However, I saw Dr. Rodriguez few weeks ago when he assured me that I was just fine. It does not mean anything but I read a previous comment where a patient expressed the same concern.

I was informed that Dr. Kandar stop processing PPO and switched for 100% fee for service MOU and I need to pay full price for my appointment. I was told that I would need to deal with my PPO insurance on my own and they would mail me a reimbursement check in 24 days!?

I was told to pay $410 for my visit. I refused and asked to see their fee schedule. It was none. Mr. Andy informed that he would clarify my fee with the doctor and would call me back later. It took several phone calls with used car dealership tactic trying to persuade me to pay inflated price. It was $410 after few phone calls it became $ 325 and finally we stopped at $ 155 for my cleaning. Again, I paid the full price and now I have to somehow receive a reimbursement check from my PPO in 24 days.  It took couple of hours and few phone calls to finalize my fee. I asked Mr. Andy to email me their fee schedule, my bill and credit card recite. I have received none.

4</rating>
<review>Beautiful mosaic steps in Sunset area of San Frsncisco. Both sides of the steps have very beautiful a d delightful garden. You can see the view of San Francisco bay and Marina district clearly on the clear day. Upon coming on top of the steps, you can climb up a zigzag stairs up to the top of the hill where the Grand View Park is located. From the Grand View Park you can see everywhere of San Francisco, down town sky line, the Golden Gate park with De Young Museum poking through, the Twin Peaks near by, the Land End etc. It is a very good experience. Best of all, it is usually not very crowded and there are plenty of roadside parking nearby with need to pay for parking.<//review>< Pictures>

It is a fabulous spot for pictures with the mosaic steps on the stairway.  Walking up and down the steps would be a good exercise for the day.  View from the top let you see the Pacific Ocean.  You will enjoy the great view during sunset.  So get your camera ready.

< review>
Beware of thieves working in groups. There was a lady out there carrying a fake baby, zipped in her coat, trying to entice people to find more stairs at the top of the staircase. There is another staircase but I'd advise you to get in the car and drive it up to the next level. Also, lock valuables in your trunk.<//review>

<user_name>Justin Link</user_name><Date>1546724716240<//Date><Rate>5<//Rate>< text>
I've been here twice. The stairs are pretty. There aren't very many of them, but interesting to see and I wish more stairs were like this elsewhere in cities. There is a spectacular view from the top, almost 360 degrees and see a lot of the city at once. Great for a sunset too. There's another small stair with mosaic nearby too. There's also a bus stop at the bottom, so you can go even if you don't have a car.</text>

<Name>Raphael Denman</Name><Time>1452308116845<//Time><rate>2</rate><Review>I don't live in San Diego, so walking in to this shop I was surprised. It is not a 'traditional' brick and mortar vapor shop. They sell only their own juice, which to be fair isn't bad. So if you're looking for a certain juice you've had before, like I was, you won't find it here. As for the quality of the product, don't expect the testers to taste like the bottle you take home. They mix the juice right there in front of you, which would be fine (cool, in fact) if it weren't for two things. First, there are no measurements taken. If your juice contains flavors such as honey, cream, marshmallow and caramel, each in specific percentages, well, all of those ingredients go into the bottle... In what appears to be a rough eyeball guesstimate. Second, since it's made right in front of you, it hasn't steeped or blended properly (not a huge deal, but it can make a big flavor difference). The staff (the one guy in there during my visit) was nice, knowledgeable and helpful, though, despite the fact that he wasn't even using the juice they make and sell there... The only real positive thing about this shop is that the prices are awesome, like half the price of premium juice at a regular retail shop.

TLDR: Low prices, but you get what you pay for.<//Review>< pictures>

<rating>1<//rating>< review>
I would love to love El Patron.  It's a cute place with lots of character and acceptable Mexican food, considering how far north we are.  I would go there more often if the service was better.  From my experience yesterday, I will never go back.  When my group walked in, the waitress practically sneered at me and didn't smile the whole time we were there. The waiter was not much better.  We waited forever to be served with no apologies and a sour face when one did show up to take our order.  There were only two servers, but it's a small place, so being understaffed is not the real issue.  When I see a staff so unhappy, I have to wonder how they're being treated by the management.  Bottom line:  I blame the management.  They deserved no tip, but I felt sorry for them and left my usual 20%.  Bad service leaves a bad taste.  Come to think of it, the food wasn't that good either.</review>

<UserId.>109031467469981826026< /UserId.><Name>J M< /Name><date>1521488568526< /date><Rating>5< /Rating><review>This place is great.

The good:

Small community feel. People know people here, and say hello and chit-chat.  The staffing at the restaurant is like a family. Treat them like your cousins, aunts and uncles, and they will, of course treat you well.  Just like anywhere, the more you get to know them, the better they treat you.
The food is good, and reasonably priced.

The "bad":
You will only find bad here if you are hyper critical. No, this is not a posh place. Go somewhere else for that. They don't do fusion menu items, it is not that kind of place.  They do get busy, because people like to connect here, so it is possible you may have to wait for 20 min mid week at dinner time.  Longer if you come on the weekend at peak dining hours.

Worth going, if you are near by.< /review><Pics>None</Pics>< Response>

<Text>This is where I go when I want true Mexican food. Despite living in Southern California melting pot, it is difficult to find good, authentic, affordable Mexican food. At last, El Patron to the rescue.

Most of the food  here is good.

Tortas? Excellent!
Carne Asada? Will tantalize your tastebuds!
Drinks! Very good

Ironically, I don't really like the tortilla chips. I've ordered them a few times to go, and they always taste like they were made with old oil.
